02/18/2020 06:48:07 PM
LogName=Security
SourceName= Microsoft Windows security auditing.
EventCode=4624
EventType=0
Type=Information
ComputerName=ACME-001
TaskCategory=Logon
OpCode=Info
RecordNumber=631083386
Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  7
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_k
 Account Name:  user_k
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xBAC3
 Linked Logon ID:  F8B0
 Network Account Name: user_a
 Network Account Domain: Domain_B
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x6531
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 129.90.7.124
 Source Port:  34014

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as DC724.exe or DC724.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 43189.exe or 43189.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  2
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_h
 Account Name:  user_h
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xA19C
 Linked Logon ID:  C183
 Network Account Name: user_l
 Network Account Domain: Domain_A
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x97A2
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 32.227.147.30
 Source Port:  51118

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 80BF8.exe or 80BF8.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 228.179.121.181

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 1679D.exe or 1679D.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM

 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  9
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Impersonation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_i
 Account Name:  user_i
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x5F25
 Linked Logon ID:  BBC3
 Network Account Name: user_m
 Network Account Domain: Domain_D
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x5EC1
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 68.161.63.172
 Source Port:  35002

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as AF53E.exe or AF53E.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3105B.exe or 3105B.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Keywords=Audit Success
Message=An account was successfully logged on.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_e
 Account Name:  user_e
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x0452
 Linked Logon ID:  4B97
 Network Account Name: user_e
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x2D30
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 142.59.46.223
 Source Port:  62627

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: -
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as A2DE0.exe or A2DE0.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3D429.exe or 3D429.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Subject:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\SYSTEM
 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

Logon Information:
 Logon Type:  4
 Restricted Admin Mode: Yes
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_h
 Account Name:  user_h
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xA19C
 Linked Logon ID:  4281
 Network Account Name: user_i
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {27C4A2F2-13CA-AA25-E903-D31268740239}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xE4D9
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  44220

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 0AACC.exe or 0AACC.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as A300F.exe or A300F.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

 Logon Type:  10
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  No

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  0F97
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: Domain_D
 Logon GUID:  {0887F1E4-39EA-D53C-804F-31D568A06274}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x8453
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_c.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 183.146.57.202
 Source Port:  59670

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 2EC96.exe or 2EC96.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 947B2.exe or 947B2.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_A

 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as AF7F9.exe or AF7F9.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_g

 Linked Logon ID:  580E
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -

 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_e.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 73.116.31.163

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  logonProcess1 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_D
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 250CE.exe or 250CE.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 23FF4.exe or 23FF4.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Account Name:  ACME-001
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: -
 Virtual Account:  No
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Delegation

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_l
 Account Name:  user_l
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0xAB37
 Linked Logon ID:  DFC8
 Network Account Name: -
 Network Account Domain: -
 Logon GUID:  {00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0xB31D
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_a.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 207.207.48.159
 Source Port:  45867

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  Winlogon 
 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 3D8CF.exe or 3D8CF.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 974A2.exe or 974A2.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Network Account Name: user_f

 Process ID:  0x92C2

 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: 35.249.248.164
 Source Port:  44387

Detailed Authentication Information:

 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 4702F.exe or 4702F.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as E7997.exe or E7997.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x70E4

 Logon Type:  11
 Restricted Admin Mode: No
 Virtual Account:  Yes
 Elevated Token:  Yes

Impersonation Level:  Identification

New Logon:
 Security ID:  Domain_A\user_n
 Account Name:  user_n
 Account Domain:  Domain_A
 Logon ID:  0x4D76
 Linked Logon ID:  B443
 Network Account Name: user_d
 Network Account Domain: Domain_D
 Logon GUID:  {221B21A6-1AE2-3F9A-24EF-22C392AC2A47}

Process Information:
 Process ID:  0x2339
 Process Name:  C:\Windows\System32\example_d.exe

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001
 Source Network Address: -
 Source Port:  1843

Detailed Authentication Information:
 Logon Process:  User32 
 Authentication Package: Negotiate
 Transited Services: service_A
 Package Name (NTLM only): -
 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 11BF9.exe or 11BF9.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as D758A.exe or D758A.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 262C0.exe or 262C0.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

Network Information:
 Workstation Name: ACME-001

Detailed Authentication Information:

 Authentication Package: Kerberos
 Transited Services: service_B

 Key Length:  0

This event is generated when a logon session is created. It is generated on the computer that was accessed.

The subject fields indicate the account on the local system which requested the logon. This is most commonly a service such as the Server service, or a local process such as 77E6B.exe or 77E6B.exe.

The logon type field indicates the kind of logon that occurred. The most common types are 2 (interactive) and 3 (network).

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.

The New Logon fields indicate the account for whom the new logon was created, i.e. the account that was logged on.

The network fields indicate where a remote logon request originated. Workstation name is not always available and may be left blank in some cases.

The impersonation level field indicates the extent to which a process in the logon session can impersonate.

The authentication information fields provide detailed information about this specific logon request.
 - Logon GUID is a unique identifier that can be used to correlate this event with a KDC event.
 - Transited services indicate which intermediate services have participated in this logon request.
 - Package name indicates which sub-protocol was used among the NTLM protocols.
 - Key length indicates the length of the generated session key. This will be 0 if no session key was requested.
